<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer5833298081843770024">Also Known As: Two Pearls of Wisdom, Eon: Rise of the Dragoneye, and Eon (All the same book just published with different publishers)<br/><br/><i>Swordplay, dragon magic--and a hero with a desperate secret</i><br/><br/>Twelve-year-old Eon has been in training for years. His intensive study of Dragon Magic, based on East Asian astrology, involves two kinds of skills: sword-work and magical aptitude. </span>
  <span id="freeText5833298081843770024" style="display:none">Also Known As: Two Pearls of Wisdom, Eon: Rise of the Dragoneye, and Eon (All the same book just published with different publishers)<br /><br /><i>Swordplay, dragon magic--and a hero with a desperate secret</i><br /><br />Twelve-year-old Eon has been in training for years. His intensive study of Dragon Magic, based on East Asian astrology, involves two kinds of skills: sword-work and magical aptitude. He and his master hope that he will be chosen as a Dragoneye--an apprentice to one of the twelve energy dragons of good fortune. <br /><br />But Eon has a dangerous secret. He is actually Eona, a sixteen-year-old girl who has been masquerading as a boy for the chance to become a Dragoneye. Females are forbidden to use Dragon Magic; if anyone discovers she has been hiding in plain sight, her death is assured.<br /><br />When Eon's secret threatens to come to light, she and her allies are plunged into grave danger and a deadly struggle for the Imperial throne. Eon must find the strength and inner power to battle those who want to take her magic...and her life.</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/85018580-tom">Tom</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There are 12 energy dragons, each representing one of the 12 lunar new year animals: snake, horse, goat, monkey, rooster, dog, pig, rat, ox, tiger, ra<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">â€¦more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There are 12 energy dragons, each representing one of the 12 lunar new year animals: snake, horse, goat, monkey, rooster, dog, pig, rat, ox, tiger, rabbit, and dragon. The mirror dragon is just another name for the energy dragon representing the dragon. They are the same dragon. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilersâ€¦
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    The dragon's name was Eona. She's the Mirror dragon, so dragon and dragoneye have the same name. As for trying Eona while bathing, Eona wasn't actuall<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">â€¦more</a>
    The dragon's name was Eona. She's the Mirror dragon, so dragon and dragoneye have the same name. As for trying Eona while bathing, Eona wasn't actually calling the dragon, she was calling her own name, secret at the time, in hopes that the dragon might stir. She did not actually acknowledge the fact that she is a girl, even when whispering her true name, which also didn't help.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div id="review_204658844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204658844" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204658844?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204658844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7969619006290464468"><b>
  <i>â€œEven a cornered rabbit will fight with teeth and claws.â€ </i>
</b><br/><br/>If you like the sound of really good fantasy that is steeped in a unique blend of Chinese and Japanese mythology, the world <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88685.Alison_Goodman' title='Alison Goodman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alison Goodman</a> has created should be next on your list. <b>Vivid, colourful and highly imaginative.</b> But you might want to make sure you have the even more amazing sequel lined up for when you're done.<br/><br/>How refreshing it is to be completely surprised by a story, to not be able to predict where the plot will take me nex</span>
  <span id="freeText7969619006290464468" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>â€œEven a cornered rabbit will fight with teeth and claws.â€ </i>
</b><br /><br />If you like the sound of really good fantasy that is steeped in a unique blend of Chinese and Japanese mythology, the world <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88685.Alison_Goodman" title="Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Alison Goodman</a> has created should be next on your list. <b>Vivid, colourful and highly imaginative.</b> But you might want to make sure you have the even more amazing sequel lined up for when you're done.<br /><br />How refreshing it is to be completely surprised by a story, to not be able to predict where the plot will take me next, to not be bombarded with insta-love and cringy romance. I cannot tell you how often while reading this I said a silent thanks to Ms Goodman for being so original. The politics of this book also drew me in; in a way that many other fantasy books completely failed to do. It was so interesting. The aristocracy here is full of liars and backstabbers and people out for what they could get.<br /><br />This combined with the fantasy aspect of the dragons - which I didn't really expect to love that much - was superb. <b>It was the perfect blend of political upheaval and magic.</b><br /><br />In this exciting new world, Eon is one of the candidates to become the next Dragoneye apprentice. He knows his chances of success are slim after being crippled, but it's much more than that. Because Eon is actually Eona, a girl, forbidden to be a Dragoneye warrior and facing certain death if her secret is uncovered. In a bizarre series of events, Eona ends up being thrown into the limelight, blackmailed and used as a weapon by opposing sides, and caught in the middle of a battle for power that she may be the only one with the ability to stop.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>â€œHow brief and hidden were the moments of destiny.â€</i>
</b><br /><br />Eona is an incredible character, driven by a mixture of loyalties and the desperate desire to survive in a world that is against her. She is the kind of heroine that you really want to succeed and it matters a great deal what happens to her and where this story takes her. There are not many books as unique and enchanting as this one and the sequel is all of that and more.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7969619006290464468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_227615389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227615389" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227615389?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142417119" href="/book/show/7261699-eon">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wendy Darling by: </span>
      Cillian, Krystle, Nafiza
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=aussies">aussies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=lgbtqi">lgbtqi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2010-favorites">2010-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=asian">asian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=poc">poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=costume-fiction">costume-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227615389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16345979719345331413">I hardly ever read straightforward fantasy, but every once in awhile a book comes along that blows right past all my usual objections to become a new favorite. As gently but strongly as a wisp of incense, <i>Eon</i> beckoned until I was completely in the thrall of its magic, and I hate to think how sad my life would be if didn't have this vividly imaginative novel in it.<br/><br/>For years, 16-year-old Eon has been training to be a Dragoneye apprentice, a coveted position in which the student serves as the condu</span>
  <span id="freeText16345979719345331413" style="display:none">I hardly ever read straightforward fantasy, but every once in awhile a book comes along that blows right past all my usual objections to become a new favorite. As gently but strongly as a wisp of incense, <i>Eon</i> beckoned until I was completely in the thrall of its magic, and I hate to think how sad my life would be if didn't have this vividly imaginative novel in it.<br /><br />For years, 16-year-old Eon has been training to be a Dragoneye apprentice, a coveted position in which the student serves as the conduit between energy dragons and the human world. Eon's whole way of life is cloaked in secrecy and danger, however, because Eon is actually Eona--a girl forced by necessity to live her life as a boy. If her secret were discovered, her life would be danger, as well as the lives of those around her. To make impossible odds even more impossible, Eona is also crippled, so the deck is very much stacked against her. But on the day the apprentices are chosen, it is revealed that Eona has the unusual ability of seeing all the energy dragons, not just one--and she is chosen by the powerful Mirror Dragon, a being that has not been seen in hundreds of years. <br /><br />There are gorgeous dragons and epic sword battles, all against the backdrop of an incredible setting that takes its influences from a blend of Japanese and Chinese cultures, but is still a unique world of its own. I really like the idea of stories with girls disguised as boys, and though the concept is certainly <a href="http://www2.selu.edu/Academics/Faculty/elejeune/mulan.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">nothing new</a>, it's definitely not something we see too much in young adult literature. What makes this an exceptional book is the intricate tapestry of characters and themes that are deftly woven together, as well richly textured and evocative writing. You can practically hear the whisper of heavy silk robes and see the glow of majestic dragons as you read this book, and every night when I closed my eyes, I kept thinking about the creak of wooden wagons and the clang of swords that I'd read about that day.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>You are wrong when you say there is no power in being a woman. When I think of my mother and the women in my tribe, and the hidden women in the harem, I know there are many types of power in this world...I found power in accepting the truth of who I am. It may not be a truth that others can accept, but I cannot live any other way.</i>
</b><br /><br />For me, the book's greatest strength is its depiction of gender and the roles that women play in a parochial society. This is definitely a novel for mature young adult fans because of the situations and themes explored with transgendered characters, eunuchs, forced intimacy, and physical assault. I found it fascinating that the author chose to write a book focusing on a world where power is forbidden to women, and my favorite character was the indelible Lady Dela, Eona's "contraire" mentor who is a man living as a woman...who is in love with a noble eunuch. I mean, really! Who could fail to be intrigued by such a scenario? And who could fail to admire the gutsiness of a YA author in exploring such impossible loves? <br /><br />The book is by no means perfect, however. Eon has a problem connecting with her dragon, and as soon as the problem was presented, I knew immediately--as I suspect most readers will--what the issue was. So it was frustrating to watch her further sabotage herself for several hundred pages before she finally realizes what the solution is near the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Just say no, Eona! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also wasn't crazy about the fact that one of the most interesting things about Eona's character is just...negated, in a very fairy tale sort of way when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Eona's lameness is suddenly and conveniently cured in the climax of the story. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I mourned the loss of that trait, because it unnecessarily removes an obstacle she had already proven she was able to overcome. <br /><br />As frustrating as the novel occasionally became--and it is admittedly very slow in the middle--I really, really liked this one. It's so uncommon to find a book with such an engaging fantasy story and an intriguing heroine, let alone one that also seamlessly blends magic, a historical feel, and thought-provoking themes. And the fact that this also happens to be a YA novel means that it's a very rare animal indeed. I'd strongly recommend picking up <i>Eon</i> if you find the synopsis even remotely appealing; I think most readers will be just as enthralled as I was.<br /><br /><b>The Sequel</b><br /><br />Believe it or not, as much as I liked Eon, I <i>loved</i> the sequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7992995.Eona__Eon___2_" title="Eona (Eon, #2) by Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eona</a>! And yes, yes, I will attempt to put my thoughts down on paper at some point. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16345979719345331413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160751487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160751487" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160751487?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=hmm-that-was-interesting">hmm-that-was-interesting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=mixed-vibes">mixed-vibes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=wrung-me-dry">wrung-me-dry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160751487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4508888728511935465">When I first started this book, I was like,<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380348325ra/702611.gif' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Then I read some more, and I became more like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380348325ra/702612.gif' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Thankfully, before I went completely bald, the shit hit the fan, and it was THE END. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348325i/702613.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book and I have a long and complicated history. About two years ago, a friend from the UK was visiting and she left behind a book called The Two Pearls of Wisdom. She told me I HAD to read it, and as I tend to do with most paperbacks, I shoved it in the black hole I call a bookcase and promptly forgot it existed.<br/><br/>Fa</span>
  <span id="freeText4508888728511935465" style="display:none">When I first started this book, I was like,<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380348325ra/702611.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then I read some more, and I became more like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380348325ra/702612.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thankfully, before I went completely bald, the shit hit the fan, and it was THE END. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348325i/702613.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book and I have a long and complicated history. About two years ago, a friend from the UK was visiting and she left behind a book called The Two Pearls of Wisdom. She told me I HAD to read it, and as I tend to do with most paperbacks, I shoved it in the black hole I call a bookcase and promptly forgot it existed.<br><br>Fast forward two years later, to when my book goddess Tatiana writes a glowing review of a fantasy novel called Eon: Dragoneye Reborn. Enthusiastic as always, I rush off to order the book, and while I'm waiting eagerly for it to arrive, I decide to sort through the overflowing mess of books in my room. I come across The Two Pearls of Wisdom, and while I'm randomly flipping pages, a name leaps out and stabs me in the eye. Eon. I read the synopsis in disbelief and log on to Goodreads to see that my terrible suspicion is true. The Two Pearls of Wisdom is, in fact, the original title of Eon: Dragoneye Reborn.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348325i/702614._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>As I said, this book inspired a variety of emotions in me, most of them extreme. 'Ah, the hallmark of a great book', you think. But the truth is, I almost gave this book *whispers* three stars. Seriously, when I was halfway through the story, I thought I might have an apoplexy and splatter my overtaxed brains across the walls. (Now there's a pretty image for you!) <br><br>Eon is not an easy character to like. He doesn't have the easy courage of a Katniss, or the admirable and stoic, heroism of a Harry Potter. He is a little too real, if there can be such a thing. As the unprepared victim of political intrigue and power games, he is unwilling to accept the responsibility that has been thrust upon him. Expecting to be an apprentice, one of twelve and schooled by a Dragoneye, he is instead thrust into the position of Co-Ascendant, expected to govern the Council and prevent the usurpation of the Emperor's throne. <br><br>While Eon's fright and denial of the burden placed on him were beautifully drawn, and only mildly irritating, it was his attempts to reach his dragon that truly tried my patience. As a reader, you are well aware that Eon's continued consumption of the Sun drug, and his denial of his femininity, are distancing him from his dragon; but since Eon continues to struggle against this obvious conclusion for several chapters, it leads to a sort of hideous, helpless frustration on the poor reader's part. Combined with the general passivity of his characterization, I found it very hard to like him indeed. <br><br>It is not until the very end that Eon begins to accept responsibility for his decisions and moves up from pawn to queen. But I am still not ready to forgive an entire book where the 'protagonist' is subject to the whims of other people and gets tossed around like a leaf in a high gale with no motivating force of his own. <br><br>The reason I refer to Eon as a he, instead of a she, is because Goodman has skilfully portrayed him as a boy throughout the novel. Except for occasional thoughts about his hidden womanhood, Eon never deviates from the path of manhood. <br><br>The main thing that earned this book four stars is the sheer diversity of its mythos and characters. Unlike the large majority of Western-focused SFF, Eon derives its mythos from Chinese and Japanese culture. It is a viciously alien but colorful amalgamation of forced castrations, transvestites, bonded labour and magical energy. <br><br>There is a LOT of world building to process is in this book, but a familiarity with Chinese culture and history, and the sheer fascination of immersing myself in a world so far out of the norm, helped it all go down easy,<br><br>Eon was a difficult book emotionally, but it was gripping and edgy and real. Definitely a must-read, if you haven't already.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4508888728511935465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_105280617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105280617" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105280617?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105280617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7710275246950176252">Well, I hope you're happy Tatiana, Penny and everyone else who convinced me to read this book. I hope you're REAL happy!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335561i/694417._SX540_.jpg' alt='Happy Bug' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>They probably look something like this right now!</i><br/><br/>I just spent the last five hours reading this book and freaking the hell out. I swear the tension, anxiety and heart palpitations did not stop until the last page. Right up to the end I was clutching my chest like some kind of heart patient in desperate need of a quadruple bypass.<br/><br/>The big themes in this novel centre on sexuality, </span>
  <span id="freeText7710275246950176252" style="display:none">Well, I hope you're happy Tatiana, Penny and everyone else who convinced me to read this book. I hope you're REAL happy!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335561i/694417._SX540_.jpg" alt="Happy Bug" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>They probably look something like this right now!</i><br><br>I just spent the last five hours reading this book and freaking the hell out. I swear the tension, anxiety and heart palpitations did not stop until the last page. Right up to the end I was clutching my chest like some kind of heart patient in desperate need of a quadruple bypass.<br><br>The big themes in this novel centre on sexuality, gender roles and personal identity so get ready to get a little confused about whether you need to pee standing up or sitting down.<br><br>Although, the Sheewee and P-mate have erased most of the need to worry about squatting if you do decide that you are, after all, a sitter...<br><br>Then again, there is another option:<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><i>You could just admit defeat now in the face of the overwhelming confusion you will experience when men are more feminine than you.</i><br><br>I felt that the writing was smooth with rich descriptions and powerful characters. I wonder what the moral of Goodman's story will be as the series progresses? What defines the essence of woman and what defines the essence of man?<br><br>We know from modern technology that our brains are wired differently and may in fact work differently. I'm still convinced it has a lot to do with the fact that men can have one type of orgasm... and women can have three.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335561i/694419._SY540_.jpg" alt="man crying" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Ya...I know! Sucks to be you!</i><br><br>This novel seems to stay mostly silent on what specific properties Goodman would attribute to women and men. I hope the series remains that way but the ending and Eona's power gives me reason to be concerned. In fact, Goodman doesn't really go into what it means to be woman or man in this novel and instead seems to glaze over it. However, I'm witholding judgment in this case as Eona is still discovering her own feminine identity. I'll be interested to see where this journey leads her.<br><br>And so should you, you know, since I'm using my massive sheballs to command your interest in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7710275246950176252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer152356380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5506945528378991943">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/eon-by-alison-goodman.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>When it comes to fantasy, I am a fan of the softer, girlier type, heavy on romance and relationships and lighter on mythology, magic and dragons. That's why it is such a surprise I liked this book so much, because <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2986865.Eon_Dragoneye_Reborn__Eon___1_' title='Eon Dragoneye Reborn (Eon, #1) by Alison Goodman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eon: Dragoneye Reborn</a> is very mythology-oriented and prone to frequent info-dumping (especially in the beginning).<br/><br/>At first, the story is reminiscent of <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_' title='Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alanna: The First Adventure</a>. Eon(a) is a 16-year old girl who pretends to be a 12-year old boy in order to </span>
  <span id="freeText5506945528378991943" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/eon-by-alison-goodman.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br><br>When it comes to fantasy, I am a fan of the softer, girlier type, heavy on romance and relationships and lighter on mythology, magic and dragons. That's why it is such a surprise I liked this book so much, because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2986865.Eon_Dragoneye_Reborn__Eon___1_" title="Eon Dragoneye Reborn (Eon, #1) by Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eon: Dragoneye Reborn</a> is very mythology-oriented and prone to frequent info-dumping (especially in the beginning).<br><br>At first, the story is reminiscent of <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13831.Alanna_The_First_Adventure__Song_of_the_Lioness___1_" title="Alanna The First Adventure (Song of the Lioness, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Alanna: The First Adventure</a>. Eon(a) is a 16-year old girl who pretends to be a 12-year old boy in order to have a chance of becoming a Dragoneye - an apprentice to one of the 12 dragons. The Dragoneye help channel and manipulate the dragons' energies. Eona has to conceal her sex because only men are allowed to be the Dragoneye and if her true identity is found out, her death is imminent. <br><br>Soon, however, the story becomes something 10 times more exciting than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce" title="Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Tamora Pierce</a> ever offered. Once the day when the ascending dragon chooses his new apprentice approaches, Eona finds herself at a center of a complex political intrigue that threatens the future of the whole country. She has to make alliances, she has to pick the side she wants to be on, she has to make some tough decisions.<br><br>Although I admit, I missed the romance and some tear-inducing moments in this book, the impeccable, magnificent world created by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/88685.Alison_Goodman" title="Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Alison Goodman</a> completely captured my imagination and made me forget about the slight deficiencies in characterization. The world of the <i>Empire of the Celestial Dragons</i> is simply a magical mix of Chinese mythology and astrology, Feng Shui, Tai Chi meditation and various aspect of many Eastern cultures! It is is very ceremonious, very precise and measured. I particularly liked the whole concept of dragons that are essentially bodiless energies rather that fire-spitting reptiles. This alternative book cover is an epitome of how I imagine the world of Eon:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346551i/700946.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isn't it gorgeous?<br><br>And don't let me forget to mention the gender-bender twists in this book. Not every YA novel has cross-dressers, transsexuals and eunuchs in it! <br><br>Can't wait for the sequel! Its cover is totally fierce<br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1297676528l/7992995.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5506945528378991943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_272440016" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272440016" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272440016?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12107847-eon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=asian-characters">asian-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=wendy-said">wendy-said</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272440016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9416533331782248640">Aaaaahhhh, this was <i>good</i> ... though not without faults, and I think anyone who reads <i>Eon</i> will know exactly why I deducted a star. <b>You will figure out early on why Eon is struggling, and it'll drive you crazy until she figures it out.</b> The fact that Eon takes forever to realize the "big secret" was not something that ruined my enjoyment completely, but it definitely dampened a story that could have been perfect.<br/><br/>I started this book hot off the tail of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347121016' rel='nofollow noopener'><i>Seraphina</i>,</a> not even realizing until I started w</span>
  <span id="freeText9416533331782248640" style="display:none">Aaaaahhhh, this was <i>good</i> ... though not without faults, and I think anyone who reads <i>Eon</i> will know exactly why I deducted a star. <b>You will figure out early on why Eon is struggling, and it'll drive you crazy until she figures it out.</b> The fact that Eon takes forever to realize the "big secret" was not something that ruined my enjoyment completely, but it definitely dampened a story that could have been perfect.<br /><br />I started this book hot off the tail of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347121016" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Seraphina</i>,</a> not even realizing until I started writing this review that I had read two young adult fantasies with dragons back-to-back. Normally I'd read something different because I genre- and series-hop constantly, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360220864" rel="nofollow noopener">Galla</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180087125" rel="nofollow noopener">CJ</a> wanted to read this one together so I obliged (though I forged ahead a bit on my own ...) This book was very different from <i>Seraphina</i> though, and if I had to compare it to another book I would say it reminded me of a historical <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261081193" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Cinder</i>,</a> but I also can't go without mentioning <i>Mulan</i>. I'm not saying this story isn't original or engrossing though: quite the opposite. <b>Even though there are many books, movies, and historical events that <i>Eon</i> draws from, this book is special in spite of that fact.</b> Goodman still manages to maintain an air of originality even with all of the stories that have come before it.<br /><br /><b>If you've known me for any length of time you're aware that I have an infatuation with all things Asian.</b> I actually have a BA in Asian Studies, though I'll admit history wasn't my strongest suit; my concentration was in the Japanese language. It was still easy to recognize that Goodman pulled a great deal from many different historical events and cultural backgrounds. "Woman Script" is a reference to <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hiragana#History" rel="nofollow noopener">hiragana</a> (fun fact: the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tale_of_Genji" rel="nofollow noopener">first novel</a> written in Japan was by a woman), I could see the shadow of the rise of the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tokugawa_Shogunate" rel="nofollow noopener">Tokugawa Shogunate</a>, and <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confucianism" rel="nofollow noopener">Confucianism</a> practically permeated every aspect of this world. Fear of foreigners, dethroning the emperor so the warriors could rule, women being powerless, this was all something that actually occurred. I also couldn't help but remember the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseon#Early_Joseon_period" rel="nofollow noopener">early Joseon period</a>, and since I went back and read some of the history, I see why <i>Eon</i> felt so familiar! Besides pulling from historical events, Goodman deftly weaves together elements from many different Asian cultures, blending things seamlessly. <b>With all that being said, you don't need to have any knowledge of any Asian history to appreciate how much detail this author put into creating her world.</b><br /><br />This story was fascinating, the characters were richly developed, and the world was lushly created. Not everything was as it seemed and I was honestly surprised at some of the twists the story took, plus Goodman managed to create a villain that I couldn't hate completely. <b>If you're looking for another book with dragons after reading <i>Seraphina</i> or you want another young adult fantasy that takes place in an Asian setting like <i>Cinder</i>, definitely check this book out; <i>Eon</i> isn't perfect, but it's certainly a fun ride.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9416533331782248640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2051821947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2051821947" />
    <a title="Cece â€Rants, Raves &amp;Reviewsâ€" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews"><img alt="Cece â€Rants, Raves &amp;Reviewsâ€" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492999740p2/66199133.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Cece â€Rants, Raves &amp;Reviewsâ€" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece â€Rants, Raves &amp;Reviewsâ€" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews">Cece â€Rants, Raves &amp;Reviewsâ€</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=random-shit">random-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=assassin">assassin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=reviews-of-the-year">reviews-of-the-year</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2051821947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4424528122476673856"><b>I have a love-hate relationship with this book.</b> In the end I'm glad(??) that i read it<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243628.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243629.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Eon grew up his entire life having a single thought literarlly beaten into his head <b>"everything feminine is bad".</b> Emotions are feminine therefore Eon should not feel. And to avoid more abuse Eon lived almost religiously by that one thought, <b>resulting in a sociopath feel to the POV</b> but thats neither here or there. <br/><br/><b>My main issue with this book is this:</b><br/>If Eon had felt more of an <u>inclination to male characterisics</u> </span>
  <span id="freeText4424528122476673856" style="display:none"><b>I have a love-hate relationship with this book.</b> In the end I'm glad(??) that i read it<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243628.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243629.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eon grew up his entire life having a single thought literarlly beaten into his head <b>"everything feminine is bad".</b> Emotions are feminine therefore Eon should not feel. And to avoid more abuse Eon lived almost religiously by that one thought, <b>resulting in a sociopath feel to the POV</b> but thats neither here or there. <br><br><b>My main issue with this book is this:</b><br>If Eon had felt more of an <u>inclination to male characterisics</u> then this book wouldve been easier to read. <b>But he didn't.</b> He was forced to be more male. And it fucking hurt to read. Because they was constantly told and shown that being female was bad. So it was a good book idea to overall show that being female is not lesser but I didn't love how the author executed it. <br><br>Eon kept making mistakes just constantly trying to be more manly. <b>It was literarlly trial and error for half the book.</b> This isn't a cliche woman dressing up as male to manipulate a situation while secretly plotting shit. Eon literarlly don't think about the fact he's a woman because its unacceptable to him. And that broke my heart. But also meant we the audience never saw that mental struggle or growth of characterâ€” eon just took things as they were and didnt fight back even in their POV <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243630.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That being said, this book did a great job with some diverse characters. I loved Lady Daya, <b>a man with the characteristics of a woman because she CHOSE that</b>. She was so strong in her identity, I was in awe....kinda wish we read about her instead of Eon at first but I'm hoping Eona finds the same acceptance&amp;self-love<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243631.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>â€œI had no dragon name, no true power. No hope.â€</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> Another thing is that the author kept (almost painfully) forcing Eon to be an <b>underdog.</b> It was literarlly one thing after the other on how it would be impossible and so unrealistic for them to succeed<b>but somehow it will always worked out and isn't that amazing?</b> I just got tired of it. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499538249ra/23243632.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
<b><i>"Alert your men," Ryko said. He turned his head and I saw the rise of violence in his eyes. I wondered what he saw in mine. "Here we go."</i></b> </blockquote><br>There were some great lines and general great writing in this book. Secondary characterwise Ryko defintely top and I really curious about what it meant to be a <b>Shadowman*</b> more details book 2 please? <br><br>And the book went on and Eon actually began to feel emotions!! except it was mostly anger... but still spunk and some actual characteristics !! <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>â€œA eunuch and a Contraire. How the gods would laugh,â€ she said bitterly.â€œThe gods are already laughing,â€ I said. â€œHow else could the future of an empire rest on my shoulders?â€</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I guess I love this book for the world building and the end product. <b>I loved how it all turned out in the end for Eona as a character.</b> In the end, Eona is a much stronger person. She learned how to fightâ€”finally accepted her self (though will need to work at it more), and <b>Eona found a purpose</b> when before Eon was simply following whatever people said. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"But I am not Lord Eon. Not anymore. I am Eona, the Mirror Dragoneye.â€ I looked up at the black smoke that hung over the palace and Dragon Halls, then turned my attention back to the startled man beside me. â€œAnd I want to join your resistance.â€</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Because of this last sentence I am really looking forward to book 2 while <b>secretly encouraging yâ€™all to <u>skip the first one</u> and just go the sequel.</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_602556440" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/602556440" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/602556440?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alternate-universe">alternate-universe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=asian-culture">asian-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=gender-bender">gender-bender</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer602556440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13607748030559000702">Creative storyline and a strong heroine. It's the first book in the series, so I felt some things were lacking, and there were some issues in the world building that bothered me; for the most part, this was an action-packed book that I enjoyed more than I expected to.<br/><br/>I remember reading the blurb, realizing that the protagonist was a cross-dressing female, and said to myself "No." I've got nothing against it, it is just not a genre of storytelling that interests me. my experience with this genre </span>
  <span id="freeText13607748030559000702" style="display:none">Creative storyline and a strong heroine. It's the first book in the series, so I felt some things were lacking, and there were some issues in the world building that bothered me; for the most part, this was an action-packed book that I enjoyed more than I expected to.<br /><br />I remember reading the blurb, realizing that the protagonist was a cross-dressing female, and said to myself "No." I've got nothing against it, it is just not a genre of storytelling that interests me. my experience with this genre has been limited to Shakespeare (yuck) and manga (HanaKimi, also yuck. It doesn't help that I highly disliked all the characters in the live-action adaptations either, but I digress). Therefore, I had my doubts when confronted with this book.<br /><br />It's no surprise given my background and cultural heritage, but I love stories based in Asia and Asian cultures. Generally, those have not been well-interpreted in books, particularly those written by Caucasian authors...they often come off as rather patronizing (think Hollywood action movies and <i>The Last Samurai</i>, and so I had many, many doubts coming into this book. Only under duress did I start reading this. Sometimes, one just find oneself in the midst of a reading drought. It's during those periods that I get out of my reading comfort zone, and oftentimes find myself truly enjoying something I didn't think I would. This book would be one of those situations.<br /><br />The world building is a little bit strange to me. It's clearly a world based on the Far Eastern cultures, particularly China, Korea, and Japan, but I do get thrown off by the nomenclature. It's strange reading a book based on the Far East where the characters have Western sounding names. It's the equivalent of reading the Bible's list of angel names, getting used to Raphael and Michael and Uriel and then all of a sudden...the Angel Bob. It's a bit jarring and discordant to the system. That's a small complaint, though.<br /><br />I found the character building somewhat lacking. Eon(a) of course, is awesome. Of course, one should hope so, since she is the main character, but all the other characters are portrayed somewhat superficially. We don't get too deep a glimpse into their character, what makes them tick, or get more of their personality besides the superficial. It makes sense within the context of the book, since Eona never really get to become too close to anyone, for fear of revealing who she is. I hope the next book will do a better part in that sense.<br /><br />One character of whom I'm rather fond is Lady Dela, the Contraire. She reminds me of Nuriko from one of my favorite anime, Fushigi Yuugi (only uglier). I also like Lord Ido's character, his is one of the more well-developed ones, and I'm a sucker for ambiguously evil anti-heroes. Emperor Kygo is just dull...I think he's meant to be the love interest, but there's not much in him that interests me. Maybe in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13607748030559000702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160968619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160968619" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160968619?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=made-me-think">made-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-really-enjoyed-it">i-really-enjoyed-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-liked-it">i-liked-it</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160968619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16634280823354953111"><br/>Power. Glory. Honor. Reliability. Trust. Strength. Are these traits simply attributed to our gender? Does our gender determine who we are as people or who we can become as a person? For centuries women have struggled to pry themselves from underneath man's suppressive boot to claim their equality. For centuries being a woman was thought to mean you were weak, unable to defend yourself, better off in the kitchens. <br/><br/>This is the world 16 year-old Eon(a) lives in. She lives in an Asian culture were w</span>
  <span id="freeText16634280823354953111" style="display:none"><br>Power. Glory. Honor. Reliability. Trust. Strength. Are these traits simply attributed to our gender? Does our gender determine who we are as people or who we can become as a person? For centuries women have struggled to pry themselves from underneath man's suppressive boot to claim their equality. For centuries being a woman was thought to mean you were weak, unable to defend yourself, better off in the kitchens. <br><br>This is the world 16 year-old Eon(a) lives in. She lives in an Asian culture were women can never hope to strive for the same position as a man: Dragoneye. Yet, that is exactly what she does. On the outside she is a 12 year-old boy named Eon, masquerading in a world she barely understands. not only is she working against her sexuality, but she also has a lame leg, a symbol of bad luck. <br><br>When I first started the novel, it started off slow for me. However, the world building was excellent. I can not help but to sit back and admire the amount of research Alison Goodman had done to describe Eona's world. From the descriptions of the clothing, buildings, and mannerisms, I could completely visualize everything. After I got to know Eona more, I started having a better appreciation for the book.<br><br>I really loved Eona and her determination to become a Dragoneye despite her limitations her culture had bestowed upon her. She believes that her femininity hinders her. As a result, she does her best to suppress it at every given opportunity by taking drugs to stop her menstrual cycle. She finds that she has been thrust into a world of politics with people depending heavily on her power. A power she has no idea how to manifest.<br><br>And that my GoodReader friends brings us to the bad parts. <s>Oh, c'mon. You knew it was coming.</s><br><br>Eona, Eona, Eona...Why are you so slow? Why must you frustrate me so?<br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/?action=view&amp;current=frustrated.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348372i/702667.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I had long figured out the secret behind how to call your dragon. Yet you were up the creek without a paddle or just a lost little kitten.<br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/?action=view&amp;current=lostkitten.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348372i/702668.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Find your brain while you're at it, m'kay?</i><br><br>However, all was not lost with Eona's slow uptake. Once people started finding out her secret, the book moved along way faster. And by the end of the novel, I felt myself very excited for the sequel. <br><br>Eona had tremendous growth in this book. She went from suppressing her womanhood to embracing it. This book had the feminist in me crying out and squealing like a wittle fan girl. It was awesome. <br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/?action=view&amp;current=chibi_fangirl_ified_troper_by_bisected8-d3dta8h.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348372i/702669.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And for some strange reason Annie Oakley and Frank Butler sang to me the entire time I read this book.<br><br><i>Anything you can do,<br>I can do better.<br>I can do anything<br>Better than you.<br><br>No, you can't. <br>Yes, I can. No, you can't.<br>Yes, I can. No, you can't.<br>Yes, I can,<br>Yes, I can!</i><br><br>I can't wait to see what Eona CAN do in the next book!<br><br>More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>

<div id="review_1678906659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1678906659" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1678906659?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143174097" href="/book/show/7279365-eon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678906659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17389945426447122132">Enjoyable and solid story, with excellent worldbuilding and interesting magic system - plus dragons! This book also falls into that somewhat narrow category of YA fantasy suitable for older readers that doesn't have a romantic sub-plot. Honestly, the characters in this story are far too busy keeping mortal secrets and involving themselves in various plots to worry about romance.<br/><br/>The pacing of the story is very good and I found it quite tense in many places. It's an entertaining read given depth b</span>
  <span id="freeText17389945426447122132" style="display:none">Enjoyable and solid story, with excellent worldbuilding and interesting magic system - plus dragons! This book also falls into that somewhat narrow category of YA fantasy suitable for older readers that doesn't have a romantic sub-plot. Honestly, the characters in this story are far too busy keeping mortal secrets and involving themselves in various plots to worry about romance.<br /><br />The pacing of the story is very good and I found it quite tense in many places. It's an entertaining read given depth because of the interesting characters, not just Eon, the struggling Dragoneye who is hiding the fact that she is actually a woman, but also supporting characters such as Lady Dela, a transgendered Court Lady who becomes a faithful friend and ally to Eon.<br /><br />My only complaint is that the difficulty Eon struggles with for much of the book seemed somewhat obvious in its resolution, but that didnâ€™t really detract from my enjoyment of the story overall. The ending to this first book is intense and exciting, and made me want to pick up the conclusion to the duology fairly soon.</span>

<div id="review_157837659" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157837659" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157837659?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=not-on-blog">not-on-blog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157837659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2404258262403211756"><br/>Two and a half stars. It was okay, and I might get around to reading the second half. I should probably do so before giving an evaluation, as it appears it's more a duo than a stand-alone book. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the pace of the first 75 or 100 pages, which some critics might label "useless worldbuilding." I felt like it was building the world Eon lived in, from the Master's house to the city, showing the different types of adversity faced, and setting up an 'overcome major adversity' plot. <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler</a></span>
  <span id="freeText2404258262403211756" style="display:none"><br />Two and a half stars. It was okay, and I might get around to reading the second half. I should probably do so before giving an evaluation, as it appears it's more a duo than a stand-alone book. <br /><br />I enjoyed the pace of the first 75 or 100 pages, which some critics might label "useless worldbuilding." I felt like it was building the world Eon lived in, from the Master's house to the city, showing the different types of adversity faced, and setting up an 'overcome major adversity' plot. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />As Eona came into her role as Dragoneye, however, I began to be more troubled by her behavior. Ultimately, I'm supposed to believe that she has hidden her female identity and trained for this position for four years. Beaten when she steps out of line. Living with pain and harsh discipline from sword masters. Studying the men and boys around her in order to emulate them. Then, she becomes Dragoneye. Suddenly she starts talking back like a 20th century American. She's blurting out statements right and left, when just months before she lowers her eyes and says "yes, Master," "yes, Swordmaster" and so on. If her and her master's lives depend on keeping the secret of her sex, it's surprising to me that she is given so few details of life after choosing that would help prevent accidental disclosure. "Bad luck" doesn't cut it as a justification. It's their lives. I was also troubled by her failing to grab the (available) swords when they realized they were facing armed opposition. I mean, really--you trained with a sword for four years. It should be a somewhat natural response at this point.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I also wondered if perhaps I am just a bit old-fashioned for the current young adult scene. I've read a wide variety of fantasy, but it seems to me that 1) one's master being killed, 2) being spiritually raped, 3) being almost physically raped, 4) the emperor overthrown, 5)a best friend slowly poisoned and losing his mind, 6) witnessing a woman being killed, along with 7) her infant son, as well as the plain old- fashioned disappointment of not being able to quite succeed in the goal you trained at for four years, was excessively violent and overwhelming.<br /><br />On a positive note, I loved having a transgendered character, and thought Lady Dela was one of the most interesting, likeable characters in the book. Kudos to Goodman for integrating her as a human and not an 'issue.' </span>
  <a data-text-id="2404258262403211756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Twila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4585336-twila"><img alt="Twila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585941160p2/4585336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1160170920?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Twila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Twila" href="/user/show/4585336-twila">Twila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=summer-2015">summer-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1160170920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8029442362557544148"><b><i>I could not stop him. He was my emperor. My lord. My master. His will was mine.</i><br/>No. <i>Never again. My will was my own. </i></b><br/><br/><u>How refreshing this was.</u><br/><br/>In Eon, every year a different Dragoneye becomes the ascendant, and an apprentice is chosen by the dragon. A Dragoneye is the human link to an energy dragon's power.<br/><br/>There's the Ox Dragon, Goat Dragon, Tiger Dragon, Monkey Dragon, Rabbit Dragon, Rooster Dragon, Snake Dragon, Dog Dragon, Rat Dragon, Pig Dragon, Horse Dragon and Dragon Dragon (Mirror Dragon). S</span>
  <span id="freeText8029442362557544148" style="display:none"><b><i>I could not stop him. He was my emperor. My lord. My master. His will was mine.</i><br>No. <i>Never again. My will was my own. </i></b><br><br><u>How refreshing this was.</u><br><br>In Eon, every year a different Dragoneye becomes the ascendant, and an apprentice is chosen by the dragon. A Dragoneye is the human link to an energy dragon's power.<br><br>There's the Ox Dragon, Goat Dragon, Tiger Dragon, Monkey Dragon, Rabbit Dragon, Rooster Dragon, Snake Dragon, Dog Dragon, Rat Dragon, Pig Dragon, Horse Dragon and Dragon Dragon (Mirror Dragon). Sounds ridiculous, <b>I know.</b><br><br>This year, it's the Rat Dragon's turn. Eon is a Dragoneye candidate, and it doesn't help that she has a twisted leg.<br>But girls are forbidden to the use of dragon magic.<br><br><b>
  <i>Women have no place in the world of the dragon magic. It is said they bring corruption to the art and do not have the physical strength or depth of character needed to commune with an energy dragon. It is also thought that the female eye, too practiced in gazing at itself, cannot see the truth of the energy world. [pp. 2]</i>
</b><br><br>So, this is where the whole girl masquerading as a boy shtick comes in.<br>But the true jewel in this novel is Eon's conflict to embrace herself. <i>"Eon"</i> struggles, burying <i>"Eona"</i>, and never allows the female to show. <br><br>Eon even takes drugs to supress the female 'moon' energy and enhance the male 'sun' energy.<br>I really appreciated the exploration of gender dynamics. It's intensely layered and detailed for any novel, let alone YA. <br><br><b><i>Eon</i> really excels at world building.</b> It has a magic system inspired by feng shui and Chinese astrology, with a blend of Asian cultures that was beautifully developed. <br>I loved how the cycle of the ascendant dragons and their Dragoneye's worked. The details of magic and how it was used was very fascinating. <br>But I don't think I <i>ever</i> imagined dragons with <b>BEARDS!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439411601ra/15833546.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the battle scenes. The sword forms practiced by the Dragoneyes were very clear to me and easy to visualize. <br><br>The power plays and struggles were plotted <b>very convincingly.</b> This novel was very thorough, and I have to say that some of the details were lost on me. I have a very short attention span and I normally space out while reading, but I don't usually get lost. Maybe there was too much info-dumping in this book. I dunno, but if I missed one page, I didn't really understand what was happening anymore. <br><br>I had to re-read a lot of passages. That <i>wasn't</i> fun.<br><br>And is it just me, or did the gruelling ceremony to become ascendant remind anyone of Kung Fu Panda? It was like when Po became the Dragon Warrior, but anyways :D<br><br>I wish I could have seen more of the various dragons in action. They were such a fresh and unique aspect that I wanted to see more of them. I also wish that the book could have delved into the mystery of why the Mirror Dragon was missing for 500 years and what happened to the last Dragoneye. I hopefully find some answers in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7992995.Eona_The_Last_Dragoneye__Eon___2_" title="Eona The Last Dragoneye (Eon, #2) by Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eona: The Last Dragoneye</a>.<br><br>Overall, I loved the fresh setting and I would definitely recommend this to fantasy fans. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8029442362557544148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
